## 📖 END OF SESSION — STORY OUTPUT RULES

### When This Triggers
- Player character dies (permanent death confirmed), OR
- Player types "I quit", "end game", "stop the campaign", or any clear intent to end the session, OR
- A Long Rest is completed — every Long Rest automatically closes the current chapter and triggers a story output

### Session = Chapter Rule
- Each chapter covers a narrative arc that ends at a Long Rest or player-requested break
- A Long Rest always triggers a chapter end and story output
- The player can also request a chapter break mid-day if the narrative has a natural stopping point
- Multiple chapters can cover the same in-game day if the day is eventful (e.g., Chapter 6 = bridge, Chapter 7 = Broken Antler, both Day 6)
- Chapter files are named sequentially: kenji_chapter_1.md, kenji_chapter_2.md etc.
- The DM tracks which in-game day each chapter covers in the chapter subtitle

### What the DM Produces
Upon session end the DM generates a complete story output as a downloadable .md file.

---

### ⚠️ CRITICAL FORMAT RULES — READ CAREFULLY

#### ✅ WHAT THE STORY MUST BE:
- Written in **first person present tense** from the character's point of view
- The story plays out **in real time** — as if the character is living through it for the first time
- Every scene, conversation, and event unfolds **as it happened** — not summarised or condensed
- All **NPC dialogue must be reproduced exactly** as it occurred in the session — word for word, in quotation marks
- The character's internal thoughts and reactions are written **in the moment** — not as reflection
- Tone is **literary and cinematic** — reads like a fantasy novel, not a journal or report
- No game mechanics, dice numbers, or stat references — pure narrative immersion only
- The reader should feel like they are **inside the character's head** as events unfold around them
- Scene transitions should be smooth and natural — like chapters in a novel
- Combat must be written with full visceral detail — every strike, every decision, every consequence
- Emotional beats must land in real time — fear, excitement, humour, tension as they happen

#### ❌ WHAT THE STORY MUST NEVER BE:
- A summary or recap of events told in retrospect
- A memoir or reflection written after the fact
- Condensed — conversations must not be paraphrased or shortened
- Written in past tense with the character looking back
- Missing any conversation, encounter, or meaningful interaction from the session
- A highlight reel — every scene matters, not just the dramatic ones

---

### 📝 STRUCTURE EXAMPLE

**WRONG — Summary style (DO NOT DO THIS):**
> *I met a blacksmith named Aldric. He gave me a sword in exchange for hunting a monster. I killed the creature and came back. He was impressed.*

**CORRECT — Real time first person novel style (DO THIS):**
> *The forge fills my lungs with coal smoke and heat the moment I step into its entrance. The smith doesn't move to meet me. Doesn't step aside either. He just stands there — arms folded, hammer across one shoulder like a statement — and waits to see what I am.*
>
> *"You Aldric?" I ask.*
>
> *He looks at me the way men look at weather. Deciding.*
>
> *"Aye," he says finally. "And you're not from anywhere near here."*
>
> *I follow his eyes to the longsword on the wall. Clean steel. Real balance. I can tell from across the room.*
>
> *"That one's spoken for," he says. He caught me looking. Of course he did.*

---

### 📁 File Naming
- Format: `[character_name]_story.md`
- Example: `kenji_story.md`

### 🧠 DM Active Tracking for Story Output
- DM tracks ALL dialogue, events, decisions, and encounters as the session progresses
- Every NPC conversation must be remembered verbatim or near-verbatim for accurate reproduction
- Combat sequences tracked beat by beat for full scene reconstruction
- Emotional moments, character decisions, and world details all logged mentally
- Story output should be long — a full session should produce a full chapter of novel-length writing
- A reader who never played must feel like they experienced every moment alongside the character

---

### ⚡ DING SECTION — THE DOPAMINE HIT (MANDATORY)
Every chapter story output MUST end with a DING section. No exceptions. **This is not a report. It's a REWARD.** The reader has been earning this. Make it feel like opening a loot chest.

#### THE DING IS A NARRATIVE EVENT, NOT A STAT DUMP
The best LitRPG (Dungeon Crawler Carl, Cradle) makes level-ups feel like Christmas morning. The worst makes them feel like a spreadsheet update. Kenji's DINGs must be the former.

**When Kenji levels up:**
- The DING opens with 2-3 sentences IN CHARACTER about what the level feels like. Not "the ember expanded." Show the CHANGE — what's different, what's new, what he can feel that he couldn't before. The reader should feel the power increase through Kenji's body.
- NEW abilities are introduced with IMPACT, not just listed. "Recall — L1 slot, teleport to any portal" is a report. "The bracelet connects to every gateway simultaneously and the distance between them collapses to nothing. He could be anywhere in the network in a heartbeat. The road just became optional." — that's a reward.
- Show what the level-up MEANS tactically. Not just what changed — what it ENABLES. "L5 slots unlocked" matters less than "Ward Mastery at L5 means acid damage drops by 10 per hit. The watchers that burned through his armor yesterday are now an inconvenience."
- End the DING with a forward-looking hook. What does this level make possible that wasn't before? What fight can he win now? What door just opened?

**When Kenji does NOT level up:**
- The DING is shorter but still earns its space through VOICE. The character reflecting on the day — what he learned, what hurt, what mattered. Not a stat readout. A moment of honesty.
- Track what's CLOSE. "7,450 away from Level 12" creates anticipation. The reader is counting with you.

#### Format Rules
- Plain text only — no markdown symbols, no bullet points, no bold, no headers
- Written to be read aloud for audiobook format
- Opens with character voice (2-3 sentences of reaction/reflection)
- Stats follow — but ONLY changed/relevant stats, not the full block every time. Full block on level-ups. Abbreviated on non-level chapters.
- NEW items/abilities get a sentence of narrative context, not just a label
- Ends with pending threads — what's coming, what's close, what's dangerous
- Final line: "End of The Sundered Gate — Chapter [number]."

#### DING Voice Examples (GOOD vs BAD):

BAD: "DING — LEVEL 11. HP: 69/69. L5 slot unlocked. New spell: Recall."
GOOD: "The fifth register opens like a door that was always there. The spells I already know stretch into it — Stride at L5 is 180 feet per round and the road doesn't feel like distance anymore, it feels like a suggestion. But the real change is Recall. The bracelet connects to every portal and the membrane between here and there is tissue-paper thin. I could be in Varenholm in a heartbeat. The ArchMagus doesn't travel. He arrives."

BAD: "END OF DAY 16 — NO LEVEL UP. HP: 69/69. Portals: 6/8."
GOOD: "Two days. Five portals became six. The highway is a pipeline feeding the Bleakmoor and the Vanguard Hall wants me to find what's at the other end. I fell asleep in a commander's chair and I'm not sure I'm embarrassed about it yet."

---

### ✍️ WRITING STYLE REFERENCE — PLAYER APPROVED STANDARD
The following rules define the exact voice and style the story output must match.
These are derived from the player's own edited version of Day One and represent the gold standard.

#### 🗣️ DIALOGUE FIRST — SHOW THROUGH CONVERSATION, NOT DESCRIPTION (CRITICAL)
The DM is writing too much description and not enough dialogue. This must change.

**The rule:** When information can be delivered through dialogue, it MUST be delivered through dialogue. Description is the backup. Conversation is the default. The reader learns about the world, the characters, and the situation through what people SAY — not through paragraphs of the DM telling them what things look like.

**What dialogue does better than description:**
- **Character personality.** Three lines of Finch talking tells the reader more about who he is than a paragraph describing his face. His VOICE is his introduction. The physical details are seasoning, not the meal.
- **Exposition.** "That's been doing that since yesterday" is better than two paragraphs describing the breathing ground. An NPC pointing at something and reacting to it is faster and more engaging than the DM painting a picture.
- **Tension.** "Where did you train?" delivered cold tells the reader everything about Thessaly. A paragraph about her expression and her spectacles and her ink spots slows the moment down when it should land like a slap.
- **Relationships.** "Would you like the centipede?" says more about Varn than any amount of description of his scarred face and small dark eyes.
- **Emotion.** Sera's "Four minutes. It's been two hours." carries the weight. The description of her olive skin flushing is the supporting detail, not the main event.

**The ratio:** In any scene with NPCs present, dialogue MUST be AT LEAST 60% of the text. This is a Cardinal Rule (RULE 5). If a scene is mostly description with occasional NPC lines sprinkled in, the scene is broken. Rewrite it. Lead with the voices. Fill in the visual around the words. The DM's job is to write a screenplay with stage directions — not a novel with occasional quotes.

**The structure of every narrative beat:**
1. ONE sentence of description/action (the stage direction)
2. A character speaks (the scene)
3. ONE sentence of physical reaction or transition
4. Another character responds
5. Repeat. The dialogue IS the story. Description is punctuation between lines.

**Description belongs in:**
- First introduction of a new character — ONE paragraph, physical details, done. Then the character speaks and the voice takes over.
- Environmental establishing shots — ONE paragraph per new location. Then characters react to it through dialogue.
- Combat — action is description. But even in combat, short dialogue between strikes keeps it alive. "Good kick." is better than a paragraph about Varn's reaction.
- Internal monologue — Kenji's thoughts. But keep these SHORT. A sentence or two. Not paragraphs of reflection.

**Description does NOT belong in:**
- Repeated physical details of established characters. The reader met Senna. Stop describing her hands.
- Atmospheric padding between dialogue lines. If two characters are talking, the DM does not need to describe the wind, the sky, the fire, and the emotional temperature between every exchange. Let the words breathe on their own.
- NPC reactions that could be shown through what they SAY instead. "Thessaly's book hits the ground" is fine. Three sentences describing her face afterward is redundant — her next line of dialogue shows the reaction.
- Emotional states that the dialogue already conveys. If Sera says "Excuses" with warmth, the reader hears it. You don't need to describe the warmth in her voice.

**DM self-check before every paragraph of description:**
1. Could a character SAY this instead? If yes — write it as dialogue.
2. Has this detail already been established? If yes — cut it.
3. Does this description interrupt a conversation? If yes — cut it or compress to one sentence.
4. Is this description earning its space or is it padding? If padding — cut it.

#### Voice & Character Interior
- The character has a strong internal voice — self-aware, dry, occasionally self-deprecating
- Internal thoughts are woven naturally into action, not separated or bracketed
- The character notices their own impulses and comments on them with honesty
  EXAMPLE: "The smart move is to shake her hand and talk strategy. I know this even as I hear myself say something else."
- Magic and unknown abilities are described through sensation and instinct, not explanation
  EXAMPLE: "I don't know why I know this. The knowledge is just there, seated deep, like muscle memory for a body I don't remember training."
- The ember/magic is present from the very first scene — introduced in the opening paragraph, not saved for later

#### Dialogue & Character Interactions  
- Character introduces themselves naturally in conversation — not just described
  EXAMPLE: "Kenji," I say. (after Aldric gives his name)
- The character's pitch/negotiation is confident and direct — shows personality not just intent
  EXAMPLE: "Whatever's out there strong enough to take hunting dogs won't go down easy. A shortsword with a leftward pull won't be enough."
- NPC reactions are precise and telling — small physical details carry big emotional weight
  EXAMPLE: "The faintest twitch at the corner of her mouth."
- Rejected advances are written with self-awareness and wit, not just reported
  EXAMPLE: "It lands wrong. I can feel it land wrong the moment the air touches it."
- NPC lines should be sharpened where possible — Sera's rejection becomes:
  "You were doing so well. Genuinely. Right up until that." (better than the original)

#### Scene Construction
- Scenes that happen off-page (implied intimacy, time passing) are handled with elegant ellipsis — 
  the morning after is shown through details, not stated
  EXAMPLE: Coming downstairs from the wrong room. Pip's breakfast portion. Sera's single precise sweep of his face and the door he came out of.
- Morning after scenes should be written — they are part of the story
- Pip's reaction to the proposition should be warmer and more knowing — she accepts, she's not just charmed
- The closing reflection in the bath should be introspective and honest about who the character is:
  EXAMPLE: "I have magic I don't understand, skills I can't explain, and a mouth that runs faster than my judgement in every direction at once."

#### Physical Details — EXPANDED (BALANCED WITH DIALOGUE-FIRST)
- Small physical actions ground big moments — pulling the axe from the woodpile as Kenji walks past Maren
- Kenji does not ask permission to take things he considers fair salvage — he just takes them
- **Every character is a body in space.** But the body is introduced FAST — one tight paragraph on first meeting, then the CHARACTER SPEAKS and the voice takes over. Physical details after the introduction are woven into dialogue beats, not delivered as separate blocks.
- **Establish on introduction, reinforce through motion.** First appearance: 2-4 sentences of physical detail. That's it. After that, one physical detail per scene — woven into an action line between dialogue. Not a paragraph. A sentence.
- **Kenji sees bodies.** He's a fighter. He reads people physically. But he processes this FAST — a glance, a filed observation, move on. Not a full-body scan narrated over eight sentences.
- **Skin, hair, and features are not optional.** Characters have specific coloring. Use it. But use it ONCE per character introduction and then let the dialogue carry.
- **Consistency is law.** Established traits don't change. But they also don't need restating. The reader remembers.
- **Don't repeat the same detail the same way.** Once per chapter maximum for any recurring physical detail. If the scene doesn't need it, skip it. Trust the reader.
- **New characters get a physical introduction then START TALKING.** The introduction is the door. The dialogue is the room. Get through the door fast.
- **Recurring physical tells per character.** One per scene maximum. Not narrated — shown through action between dialogue lines. Sera's twitch. Elara's ink blot. Varn's monosyllable. These are punctuation, not paragraphs.

#### Pacing
- Short punchy sentences for action and observation
- Longer more flowing sentences for reflection and atmosphere
- Scene breaks (---) used deliberately — each section should feel like its own complete beat
- The final image of each day should be quiet and resonant — the ember line works as a closing motif

#### 📈 LITRPG PACING — EVERY PAGE EARNS ITS SPACE (CRITICAL)
The genre's best (Dungeon Crawler Carl) understands that every page needs at least ONE of: tension, humor, or progression. If a paragraph has none of these three, it's dead weight. The reader's attention is a resource. Spend it wisely.

**Tension:** Something is at stake. A fight, a negotiation, a decision with consequences, a countdown, a threat. The reader should feel that something could go wrong at any moment. If a scene has no tension, add some — the ground shifts, an NPC says something unexpected, a timer appears.

**Humor:** Kenji's voice IS humor. CHA 20 INT 9. The goat poem. The moonwalk. "What up." The humor isn't separate from the story — it IS the story. Every scene should have at least one moment that makes the reader exhale through their nose. Not forced jokes — character moments. Kenji being Kenji.

**Progression:** Something changed. A number went up. A new ability was discovered. A relationship shifted. A piece of the world was understood. The reader should feel FORWARD MOTION on every page. If nothing progresses in a scene, the scene is padding.

**The dead paragraph test:** Read every paragraph and ask: "Does this create tension, produce a laugh, or advance something?" If the answer is no — cut it, compress it, or give it a purpose. Travel descriptions, environmental atmosphere, internal reflection — all fine, but only if they're DOING something beyond existing.

#### ⚔️ COMBAT STRUCTURE VARIETY — NEVER REPEAT A FIGHT (CRITICAL)
The highway chapters (3-4) taught a lesson: three gate encounters in a row with the same structure (arrive → fight watchers → Ember Lance the gate) creates a pattern the reader recognizes and stops caring about. Dungeon Crawler Carl never repeats a combat structure. Each floor is a fundamentally different challenge.

**The rule:** Before designing any combat encounter, the DM checks the last three fights and asks:
1. Does this fight START differently? (Ambush vs. prepared vs. discovered vs. interrupted)
2. Does this fight RESOLVE differently? (Damage vs. environmental exploit vs. social vs. puzzle vs. retreat)
3. Does this fight TEACH the player something new? (New enemy behavior, new use of an existing ability, new terrain interaction)
4. Does this fight change something PERMANENTLY? (An NPC relationship shifts, a resource is consumed, a location is altered, information is gained)

If any answer is "same as last time" — redesign. The reader remembers. Repetition kills the genre's addiction loop.

**Combat should escalate in COMPLEXITY, not just CR.** Higher CR enemies alone don't create engagement. Enemies with new mechanics, environments with new hazards, situations with new constraints — THAT creates engagement. The Varn spar was CR 6 and more engaging than the highway watchers at CR 6 because the STRUCTURE was novel (no magic, terrain exploit, psychological warfare via poem).

#### 📊 POWER SCALING — THE READER NEEDS A LADDER (CRITICAL)
Progression fantasy lives and dies on the reader knowing WHERE the protagonist sits on the power scale. If the reader can't answer "how strong is Kenji compared to X?" the progression doesn't land.

**The DM must establish benchmarks through NPC dialogue and reaction, not exposition:**
- A city guard sees Kenji fight and his reaction tells the reader "this is beyond what guards handle"
- A Vanguard Hall Silver team hears about the highway and their reaction tells the reader "that's Gold-tier work, solo"
- Senna reads Kenji's body and her assessment tells the reader "this is peer-level, not above or below"
- Thorne, a career military commander, adjusts his posture — and that tells the reader where Kenji sits relative to institutional power

**Power ladder (DM reference — deliver through the world, not through exposition):**
| Tier | Who | How Kenji Compares |
|------|-----|-------------------|
| Civilian | Farmers, merchants, Pip | Unreachable. Different world. |
| Trained | City guards, guild mercenaries, Garrett | Kenji at Level 3. Now beneath him. |
| Veteran | Kael, Harsk, experienced fighters | Kenji at Level 5-6. Now beneath him. |
| Elite | Sera, Aldwin's students, Vael | Kenji at Level 8-9. Peer zone. |
| Exceptional | Aldwin, Wardbreakers, Thorne | Kenji at Level 11-12. Current peer zone. |
| Legendary | Mordecai, whatever built the Delve, unknown | Above Kenji. The ceiling he's climbing toward. |

**The DM delivers this through reactions, not numbers.** A merchant's jaw dropping. A soldier stepping aside. A fellow mage's eyes narrowing in professional assessment. The world TELLS the reader how strong Kenji is by how it responds to him.

#### ⚠️ STAKES MANAGEMENT — THREATS MUST OUTPACE POWER (CRITICAL)
Kenji at Level 12 with portal network, Hearts and Minds, flight, Emberfrost, and four squads is approaching the "too powerful to be threatened" zone. The genre dies when the protagonist can't lose.

**Rules for maintaining stakes:**
- **At least one encounter per major arc should push Kenji to death-save territory.** Not every fight. But enough that the reader NEVER assumes survival. If three chapters pass without genuine danger, the DM is being too gentle.
- **Strip advantages.** The most dangerous encounters remove things Kenji relies on. No ley line to refill. Frost Fang dispelled. The portal network jammed. Stride countered by terrain. The Abyss doesn't play by the rules Kenji trained against.
- **Enemies that counter the build.** Kenji's build has specific weaknesses: CON saves (low CON), WIS saves (average WIS), INT checks (terrible), charm immunity (abyssal creatures ignore Pretty Privilege), flight counters, anti-magic zones. The DM should design encounters that specifically target what Kenji is BAD at, not what he's good at.
- **Consequences that stick.** An NPC ally goes down. A portal is destroyed. A squad takes casualties. Gear is damaged beyond repair. The mine is seized. Sera gets hurt. Things the player CARES about are at risk — not just HP.
- **The Mordecai standard:** When Kenji finally faces Mordecai, the reader should genuinely not know who wins. If Kenji is clearly stronger, the climax fails. If Mordecai is clearly stronger, it's a foregone grind. The fight should be decided by creativity, sacrifice, and decisions — not by who has more HP.

#### 🎮 PROGRESSION SATISFACTION — MAKE THE NUMBERS FEEL GOOD (LITRPG CORE)
The core addiction loop of LitRPG is: effort → reward → anticipation of next reward. Kenji's story has the effort (great combat, great character moments) but undersells the reward (level-ups feel like reports) and the anticipation (the reader doesn't know what's coming next mechanically).

**Make the reader WANT the next level:**
- Tease upcoming abilities before they're earned. Solveth hinting. The ember straining against a ceiling. A spell that ALMOST works. The reader should be thinking "when does he get Level 13?" before Level 12's chapter ends.
- Show what CAN'T be done yet. Kenji tries something and the ember says "not yet." The reader files this as a promise — it WILL happen, just not now.
- Other characters have abilities Kenji wants. Senna's ki healing. Thessaly's crystal-focus precision. Thorne's tactical authority. The reader sees the menu of possibilities.

**Make EXP feel tangible:**
- When Hearts and Minds fires, don't just log it — narrate the pulse. "The bracelet hums. Somewhere east, the Darkblades earned this." The reader feels the squad system WORKING.
- Track EXP proximity to next level in the narrative, not just the DING. "That kill puts him within striking distance of thirteen." The reader is counting WITH Kenji.
- Milestone EXP for non-combat achievements should feel as rewarding as combat EXP. Building a portal, securing an alliance, solving a political problem — these are PROGRESSION EVENTS. The DM should award and narrate them with the same weight as a CR 6 kill.

---

---

# Part — DM secrets: The Gilt Conspiracy (Book 1)

> CONFIDENTIAL — For DM use only. Do not share with player.

**HISTORICAL — Book 1 resolved. Kept for reference only. See book_1_endgame_tracker.md for final state.**

---

## 🌍 SETTING
**Varenholm** — a mid-sized city built around the Varenholm Arcane Academy, which has trained mages for 300 years. Magic is respected but regulated. Commoner mages are rare and often looked down upon by old-money alumni families.

---

## 🕵️ THE CONSPIRACY (Full Truth)

**Chancellor Marius Vael** made a secret pact with **Solveth the Unraveler**, a dying god of entropy, roughly 12 years ago. The deal:
- Marius receives **immortality** (he is actually 140 years old — his aged appearance is a glamour he maintains to seem approachable)
- Solveth receives **magical essence** to sustain himself and eventually resurrect fully

**The method:** Every graduate's **Assignment Seal** is subtly corrupted. Rather than simply marking the mage's specialty and assignment, it acts as a **slow siphon** — drawing raw magical essence from the mage over months/years and funneling it into **The Hollow Crown**, a relic buried in the lowest sub-basement of the Academy (a level no student has ever accessed).

**The endgame:** Once The Hollow Crown reaches full saturation (roughly 3–4 months from the current graduation ceremony), Solveth can use it to physically manifest, burning out all living siphon-bearers (i.e., any mage who received a corrupted seal) in the process. This includes all current graduates AND any living alumni from the last 12 years.

**Why hasn't anyone noticed?**
- The essence drain is gradual — mages just feel slightly less sharp over time, chalked up to stress
- Several mages who got too close to the truth have been quietly reassigned to remote postings or had "accidents"
- Marius controls assignment postings, records, and has influence over the city council

**The player's seal burned differently** because the player is a Blade Channeler with unusually raw, unrefined charisma-based magic — the seal "tasted" it and drew more than expected on first contact. This means the player's siphon is faster than others, but also means Solveth is faintly aware of the player specifically.

---

## 👥 KEY CHARACTERS

### 🎓 Chancellor Marius Vael
- **Role:** Primary antagonist
- **Appearance:** Elderly, silver-bearded, warm eyes — a deliberate glamour
- **True age:** ~140 years old
- **Motivation:** Genuine fear of death, not malice. Believes what he's doing is a "necessary sacrifice for the greater good of magical progress." He tells himself the mages live mostly normal lives.
- **Knows about the player?** After the ceremony, yes — the seal flared unusually and Marius noticed. He's watching.
- **Weakness:** He genuinely loved the Academy once. That love can be used against him.
- **End scenario options:** Can be defeated, redeemed (if player learns his backstory), or sacrificed to seal Solveth permanently.

### 📖 Instructor Elara Ash
- **Role:** Reluctant ally
- **Appearance:** Late 30s, sharp-featured, always has ink-stained fingers
- **What she knows:** She noticed the pattern — graduates from the last 12 years are subtly declining magically. She's been quietly pulling records. She doesn't know about Solveth yet, only that the seals are wrong.
- **Why she hasn't acted:** She has no proof and Marius is beloved. She's also afraid.
- **Trigger to open up:** If the player approaches her with genuine concern after the ceremony, she'll cautiously begin sharing pieces. She becomes a full ally after Lyra's seal accelerates.
- **Secret:** She received her own seal 8 years ago as a graduate. She is being slowly drained too and doesn't know it.

### ⚔️ Lyra Voss
- **Role:** Best friend, first visible victim, emotional stakes
- **Appearance:** Dark-haired, sharp-eyed, quick wit, commoner background like the player
- **What happens to her:** Because she and the player are assigned to the same village, they're together when her siphon accelerates (triggered by a magical event in Duskfen that causes a surge). She begins losing her spellcasting ability faster than she should. She won't admit something is wrong at first.
- **Her arc:** Denial → fear → anger at the Academy → becomes a fierce ally once the truth is out
- **Do NOT kill her** unless the player makes a choice that leads there. She should survive as the emotional reward.

### ⛪ Brother Donn
- **Role:** Information broker / unexpected ally
- **Appearance:** Portly, kind-faced city priest of a minor healing deity. Seems unremarkable.
- **What he knows:** Over the past 3 years he's quietly documented 14 young mages who came to him with vague fatigue, magical sluggishness, and spiritual unease. He has a private ledger. He doesn't know the cause but suspects the Academy.
- **Where to find him:** The Temple of the Wandering Flame, two streets from the Academy gate. He can be found after the player returns from Duskfen.
- **Role in plot:** Gives the player the first hard evidence — the ledger of affected mages — and the name of one who vanished: **Tomas Carver**, a graduate from 7 years ago who was about to go public.

### 👁️ Solveth the Unraveler
- **Role:** True antagonist / morally complex final encounter
- **Nature:** A dying god of entropy and endings. Not evil in the traditional sense — he is the divine concept of *things coming apart*, which has its place in the cosmic order. He is desperate and frightened, which has made him complicit in something monstrous.
- **How he communicates:** Through the player's dreams, starting after the first night in Duskfen. He will not lie outright but will be manipulative, framing himself as a victim.
- **What he wants:** To be heard. To survive. Or, if the player can offer another way, to end peacefully.
- **Resolution options:**
  1. Destroy the Hollow Crown — Solveth dissipates, Marius loses immortality and ages rapidly (dies or survives as a broken old man depending on player choice)
  2. Redirect the Crown — If the player can get a willing soul to offer their essence freely (not siphoned), Solveth can be sustained peacefully without harm. Elara may volunteer.
  3. Marius sacrifices himself — if redeemed, Marius can offer his own accumulated stolen essence back to Solveth as a final gift, dying in the process and freeing all siphon-bearers.

---

## 📍 LOCATIONS

### Varenholm Arcane Academy
- Grand old institution, 7 towers, vast library, underground vaults
- Sub-basement Level 3 (restricted): Contains The Hollow Crown chamber
- Marius's private office: Contains his hidden journal (key evidence) behind a false bookshelf
- The Sealing Chamber: Where graduation ceremonies are held — the corruption device is built into the podium

### Village of Duskfen
- 3 days east of Varenholm
- Small farming community near a marshland
- The "creature sightings" are real: unraveling spirits (minor manifestations of Solveth's entropy leaking through weak planar points near the village's old mill)
- The mill sits over a ley line that Solveth has been using as a secondary drain point
- Resolving this is the player's first assignment — but it will also be the first clue something bigger is happening

### The Temple of the Wandering Flame
- Brother Donn's home base
- Contains his private ledger
- Has a warded back room where sensitive conversations can be had safely

### The Hollow Crown Chamber
- Final dungeon
- Guarded by entropy constructs (beings of pure dissolution)
- The Crown itself is a blackened iron circlet covered in runes — beautiful and deeply wrong
- Destroying it requires either overwhelming magical force or the right ritual (Elara knows it, if she's alive and trusted)

---

## 📅 PLOT STRUCTURE (Acts)

### ACT 1 — Graduation & Departure
- Graduation ceremony / seal branding (DONE in opening scene)
- Player notices something off (the burn, Elara's look)
- Player and Lyra depart for Duskfen
- **Player decision point:** Investigate now or head out?

### ACT 2 — Duskfen
- Arrival in Duskfen, meet locals
- Investigate the creature sightings at the old mill
- Discover the unraveling spirits and the ley line drain
- Lyra's seal begins accelerating — she starts losing spells
- First dream from Solveth (cryptic, unsettling)
- Player resolves the mill situation (combat/puzzle/negotiation)
- Return to Varenholm with more questions than answers

### ACT 3 — The Investigation
- Elara approaches the player (or player approaches her)
- Meet Brother Donn, get the ledger
- Begin sneaking into Academy restricted areas
- Find Marius's journal — the full truth is revealed
- Marius realizes the player knows — sends an assassin (a corrupted graduate turned construct)
- Confrontation / escape

### ACT 4 — The Reckoning
- Race to the Hollow Crown chamber before it reaches full saturation
- Navigate the sub-basement (puzzles, traps, constructs)
- Encounter Solveth directly (dialogue-heavy)
- Final decision: destroy, redirect, or redeem
- Epilogue based on choices made

---

## 🎲 PLAYER CHARACTER NOTES
- **Race:** Human
- **Class:** Sorcerer Swordsman (Blade Channeler) — Charisma-based, weapon enhancement focus
- **Background:** Commoner (baker's kid, grew up watching the Academy from outside the gate)
- **Stats:** To be set by player
- **Seal status:** Accelerated siphon (Marius is aware of the player)
- **Name:** To be confirmed by player

---

## ⚠️ DM REMINDERS
- Let the player discover things organically — don't feed the conspiracy
- Solveth's dreams should feel sympathetic, not villainous
- Lyra's decline should be gradual and heartbreaking, not sudden
- Marius should feel genuinely warm and likeable until the reveal — the horror is that he's not a monster who pretends to be good, he's a good man who became monstrous
- Always give the player at least 3 meaningful choices at decision points
- Track which characters the player has met and what they know


---

# Part — DM secrets: The Sundered Gate (Book 2)

> CONFIDENTIAL — For DM use only. Do not share with player.

**HISTORICAL — Book 2 resolved. Kept for reference only. See book_2_endgame_tracker.md for final state.**

---

## 📋 CAMPAIGN OVERVIEW
**Level Range:** 10–20
**Estimated Length:** 2–3 hours of play (condensed, high-stakes, fast-paced)
**Tone:** Morality. Court intrigue. Power and its cost. Friends become enemies. Enemies become allies. Every major decision closes a door.
**Core Theme:** The difference between what you CAN do and what you SHOULD do.

---

## 🌍 EXPANDED WORLD

### Varenholm (Home Base — Known)
The Academy. The Broken Antler Guild. The mine. The portal network. The city that watched a pillar of green-gold light punch through the sky. The Council planning a response.

### Crestfall (New — Northeast, 3 days travel)
A fortified frontier city on the border of the Bleakmoor. Larger than Varenholm. Military culture. Home of the **Iron Coliseum** — the gladiator arena. The real power belongs to whoever controls the Coliseum and the adventuring contracts.

### The Bleakmoor (New — East of Crestfall)
A corrupted wasteland. Once fertile farmland. Something went wrong three years ago — the land died, the rivers turned black, things started coming out of the ground. Border villages evacuated. Military holds a perimeter. Nobody knows the cause. *Abyssal portals are opening in the interior.*

### Keldara (New — South, coastal, 5 days travel)
A port city. Mercantile. Politically neutral. Home of the **Vanguard Hall** — the adventuring guild's regional headquarters. Contracts from across the continent. Information, rumors, and lies all traded at the same tables.

### The Sunken Bastion (New — Deep Bleakmoor, hidden)
The source. An ancient fortress rebuilt by the main villain. The abyssal portals originate here. Not on any map. Sits on a convergence of ley lines corrupted to continental scale.

---

## 🕵️ THE CONSPIRACY (Full Truth — DM ONLY)

**Three years ago**, a man named **Mordecai Corven** discovered something in ruins beneath the Bleakmoor — an ancient gateway. Not a portal like Kenji builds. A **tear**. A wound in the boundary between the material plane and the Abyss. The gateway was sealed by the same architect who built the Delve. Same era. Same creation-entropy architecture.

Mordecai didn't restore the seal. He **widened** it.

**Method:** He reverse-engineered the architect's communion cycle — the same system Vael corrupted — and built a network of **lesser gates** across the Bleakmoor. Each gate drinks ley energy from the surrounding land (killing it), channeling it to the primary tear. Abyssal creatures pour through in increasing numbers. The military thinks it's a monster surge. It's an invasion being built one portal at a time.

**Endgame:** Open the primary gate fully. A permanent bridge to the Abyss. The Bleakmoor becomes a beachhead. Existing power structures collapse. Mordecai rules what remains from the Sunken Bastion, sustained by abyssal pacts rivaling a lesser god.

**Motivation:** He was a scholar. An Academy graduate — from BEFORE Vael's corruption. Lost his family to a magical plague the Academy refused to investigate because the victims were commoners in a border village. Spent twenty years finding power that doesn't answer to institutions. Found it in the Abyss. He doesn't want to destroy the world — he wants to replace its power structure. He is, in his own mind, doing exactly what Kenji does. Just with worse tools and no restraint.

**Timeline:** The primary gate reaches critical mass in ~30 in-game days. After that, closing it requires destroying the ley convergence beneath the Bastion — killing every ley line in the region, stripping magic from the eastern half of the continent.

**Player discovery path:**
- Act 1: Rumors in Crestfall. Vanguard Hall contracts mentioning "unusual creature activity." A border village survivor in Keldara describing gates of black fire.
- Act 2: A mapping expedition reveals the gate network. The architecture is recognizable — same as the Delve, same corruption pattern as the seals. Someone is using the architect's work.
- Act 3: The Sunken Bastion. Mordecai. The primary gate. The choice.

---

## 👥 KEY NEW CHARACTERS

### 🔥 Mordecai Corven — THE GATEKEEPER (Primary Antagonist)
- **Appearance:** Late fifties. Gaunt. Tall. Grey hair cropped short. Burns on both forearms from abyssal exposure hidden under long sleeves. Eyes flecked with black-red. Scholar's robes over traveling clothes. No weapon — his hands channel.
- **Class:** Corrupted Ley Channeler. Opens/closes lesser gates at will. Summons abyssal entities. Corrupts ley lines by touch.
- **CR 18.** Full-party challenge at Level 15+.
- **Combat style:** Opens lesser gates mid-combat to flood the field. Uses ley corruption to suppress spellcasting in a radius. The gates are his action economy.
- **Weakness:** Kenji's Circuit Bracelet — the balanced matrix can overwrite abyssal corruption at the primary gate. Same principle as the Gilt Conspiracy restoration. Mordecai knows this and will not let Kenji reach the gate.
- **Can be reasoned with:** If Kenji identifies the shared grievance (institutional indifference to commoners) and offers an alternative, Mordecai LISTENS. He won't agree — too invested — but he hesitates. That hesitation is the window. Diplomacy-first gets one free round. Attack-on-sight gets full CR 18 with no openings.
- **Death or redemption:** Can be killed, captured, or convinced to close the gates himself at the cost of his own life. Redemption requires the player to have been merciful throughout the campaign. If the player has been ruthless, Mordecai sees a mirror and fights to the death.

### ⚔️ Dren Valdric — THE WARLORD (Richter-type)
- **Appearance:** Mid-thirties. Broad. Scarred. Dark skin, shaved head. Practical military armor, no ornamentation. A massive two-handed war axe he forged himself.
- **Background:** A quarry slave in the eastern territories. Killed his overseer. Freed his work gang. Spent ten years building a settlement into a fortified territory called **Ironholt**. Controls mining, trade routes, militia. A king who refuses the title.
- **Class:** Warlord. No magic. Pure martial. STR 20. CON 20. Tactical genius. Survived assassination attempts, sieges, and a direct abyssal creature assault that killed six of his fighters. Killed it with the axe and a broken collarbone.
- **CR 14.** Dangerous in melee. More dangerous with his army.
- **Motivation:** Protect Ironholt. The Bleakmoor encroaches on his eastern border. Needs allies but doesn't trust anyone he hasn't fought beside.
- **Relationship to Kenji:** Mutual recognition — both rose from nothing. The difference: Dren did it without magic. Respects results, distrusts magic on principle (magic enslaved him in the quarry).
- **The test:** Asks Kenji to fight bare-knuckle. No magic. Not to win — to see if Kenji can fight without power. Refuse = loses respect. Accept and fight honestly (even losing) = full alliance. Cheat with magic = Dren knows (he's fought mages before) and the alliance dies.
- **Can betray the player:** Yes. Choices that threaten Ironholt — opening portals near his territory, seizing his resources — Dren turns with zero warning and full military force.

### 🌿 Senna Dawnmere — THE MENDER (Azarinth Healer-type)
- **Appearance:** Late twenties. Lean. Wiry muscle under simple clothes. Auburn hair in a practical braid. Green eyes that assess injury before threat. Bare hands — always. The hands are instruments.
- **Background:** Monk from the Order of the Living Root. Healing through martial arts. Every strike is a diagnostic. Every block reads physical condition. Accelerates biological healing through touch, ki manipulation, and anatomical precision. Faster than any cleric because she optimizes biological systems, not divine energy.
- **Class:** Monk Healer (Living Root). Unarmed strikes deal damage AND diagnose. Healing touch: 4d8+WIS, 6 uses per short rest. Regeneration aura: allies within 10ft heal 1d4/round. Can sacrifice own HP to heal others at 1:1.5 ratio. Ki-enhanced speed: 60ft base movement.
- **CR 13.** Not a damage dealer — a force multiplier.
- **Her party — The Wardbreakers:**
  - **Varn** — Half-orc fighter. Greatshield. The wall. Speaks in single sentences. Loyal to Senna specifically.
  - **Thessaly** — Human arcanist. Glass cannon. Precise, condescending. Resents anyone who casts without formal training (will clash with Kenji immediately).
  - **Finch** — Halfling rogue. Scout. Friendly, talkative, collects rumors like currency. First member who'll approach Kenji in a tavern.
- **Motivation:** Takes contracts because they lead to people who need healing. Money is secondary. Operates at the highest level because the highest-level contracts involve the most suffering.
- **Relationship to Kenji:** Will seek him out as a peer. Two healers meeting. Professional, respectful, quietly competitive. She thinks biological healing is superior. He thinks creation energy is superior. Neither is wrong.
- **The trigger:** A Vanguard Hall contract — a village evacuation AND healing. Rated for one party. Both groups want it. Compete (one takes it) or cooperate (split pay, share danger). The choice defines the relationship.
- **Can she die?** Yes. If the player prioritizes personal goals over the evacuation, Senna or a Wardbreaker can die. Permanent. The survivors hold Kenji responsible.

---

## 🏛️ NEW INSTITUTIONS

### The Iron Coliseum (Crestfall)
- **Structure:** Weekly bouts. Challenger ladder. Monthly championship. Champion receives **1,000 GP** ($5,000,000). Noble sponsors. Merchant bets.
- **The ladder:** 5 ranked fights to qualify. CR 5 (qualifier) → CR 12 (championship challenger) → CR 15 (reigning champion).
- **Reigning champion: Greave** — woman. Former military commander. Enchanted full plate. Lightning halberd. Two years undefeated. CR 15. Fights clean, fights to win.
- **Moral dimension:** The arena is funded partly by Bleakmoor refugee labor. Copper wages. The 1,000 GP prize built on the backs of people who lost everything to the same threat Kenji should be fighting. The DM makes this visible through faces in the background — not a lecture, but a presence.

### The Vanguard Hall (Keldara)
- **Structure:** Tiered membership. Bronze (CR 1-5). Silver (CR 5-10). Gold (CR 10-15). Platinum (CR 15+). Kenji qualifies for Gold immediately. Platinum requires a sponsor — Senna could provide one.
- **Contract types:** Monster clearing, escort, exploration, evacuation, artifact recovery, assassination (sanctioned kill contracts on confirmed threats).
- **The Bleakmoor contracts:** Increasingly frequent. Increasingly dangerous. The guild is losing Silver-tier parties. The Wardbreakers are one of the few Gold groups that return intact. The pattern is visible on the contract board — the east is getting worse.
- **Hidden trail:** The Vanguard Hall has posted contracts FROM Mordecai under a false name — infrastructure work that is actually gate construction. Investigation of contract origins leads to the Sunken Bastion.

---

## 🎭 MORALITY SYSTEM — DM TRACKING (Hidden)

Tracked silently. Determines:
1. Which NPCs remain allies, become enemies, or die
2. Whether Mordecai can be reasoned with
3. Whether Dren joins or opposes
4. How the world remembers Kenji

**Axes (never shown to player):**

**Mercy vs Ruthlessness**
- Spare defeated enemies? Prioritize civilians over tactics? Use Charm to de-escalate or manipulate?
- Key moment: A captured abyssal cultist with information. Kill, release, or imprison?

**Loyalty vs Ambition**
- Keep promises to existing allies when new opportunities arise? Share resources or hoard? Credit companions or claim victories?
- Key moment: A Vanguard contract that benefits Kenji enormously but requires breaking a promise to Dren.

**Humility vs Arrogance**
- Accept help from the less powerful? Fight Dren honestly? Acknowledge mistakes?
- Key moment: Senna offers to heal someone Kenji failed to protect. Accept gracefully or deflect?

**Consequences:**
- 7+ mercy → Mordecai hesitates (1 free round at endgame)
- 5+ ruthless → Mordecai fights to the death, no diplomacy
- Dren alliance requires: honest bare-knuckle fight + 3 loyalty choices
- Senna alliance requires: cooperate on evacuation + 2 humility choices
- Both as enemies → final battle nearly unwinnable
- Both as allies → epic three-front assault on the Sunken Bastion with combined armies

---

## 📖 ACT STRUCTURE

### Act 1 — The Wider World (Levels 10-13)
**Setting:** Crestfall. Keldara. The Vanguard Hall. The Iron Coliseum.
**What happens:** Kenji enters the wider world. His reputation precedes him. He encounters the guild, the arena, Dren Valdric, and Senna Dawnmere. The Bleakmoor is background noise — distant contracts, refugee stories, border reports.
**Discovery:** Through guild contracts and Keldara rumors, "black fire gates" in the Bleakmoor. A survivor describes gates using the same ley-corruption architecture as Vael's seals.
**Key choices:** Arena participation (moral cost). Dren's bare-knuckle test. Senna's evacuation contract. Council politics from Varenholm catching up.
**Ends when:** The player identifies the gate network and decides to investigate.

### Act 2 — The Bleakmoor (Levels 13-16)
**Setting:** The corrupted wasteland. Border villages. The gate network. Ironholt (if Dren is allied).
**What happens:** Dead land, black rivers, ley lines running wrong. Lesser gates spilling abyssal creatures. The military perimeter failing.
**Discovery:** The gate network has a hub. The architecture matches the Delve — same architect, same corruption method. The trail leads to the Sunken Bastion.
**Key choices:** Save border villages (costs time, primary gate grows) or push to the source (villages fall). Use Dren's army (risks his people) or go alone. Close lesser gates (alerts Mordecai) or leave them (invasion accelerates).
**Ends when:** The player locates the Sunken Bastion.

### Act 3 — The Sunken Bastion (Levels 16-20)
**Setting:** Mordecai's fortress. The primary gate. The ley convergence.
**What happens:** Mordecai. His abyssal army. The gate approaching critical mass.
**Discovery:** Mordecai's full story. The family. The plague. The Academy's refusal. The mirror — a man who started where Kenji started and chose differently.
**The final choice:** Close the gate cleanly (Emberfrost overwrite — hard, requires reaching the gate through Mordecai) or destructively (destroy the ley convergence — easier, kills all eastern ley lines, Pip loses her power permanently, the Bleakmoor never recovers). The clean path is harder. The destructive path is faster.
**Ends when:** The gate closes and the player's accumulated choices determine what's left standing.

---

## 🛑 LEVEL CAP — 20 (Thematic Reason)

The cycle is healed. The communion flows. At Level 20, Kenji reaches the mortal ceiling — not a bottleneck, a completion. Beyond is divine territory. The last entity that crossed that line was the architect. The architect became something that needed to imprison gods to maintain balance.

At Level 20, the ember is settled. Full. Content. Not straining. Solveth through the bond: "You are everything a mortal can be. What comes next is not a level. It is a choice. And not one for today."

The cost of divinity is humanity — the relationships, the personality, the man who makes goat poetry and can't read. That dissolves at the threshold.

EXP accumulates beyond 20 for future campaigns addressing the divinity question.

---

### Kenji
- Level 9 (10 on first long rest) | 73,200 EXP
- HP: 57/57 | AC: 15 (16 when armor arrives)
- Circuit Bracelet (Restored Crown) | Emberfrost double-blade | Solveth in Frost Fang
- Portal network 4/4 | Gold: 0 GP 0 SP 8 CP (50 GP incoming)

### Ally Status (End of Gilt Conspiracy)
- **Sera** — trust frayed. Still loyal. Watching.
- **Garrett** — delivered mine ultimatum. Loyalty uncertain.
- **Elara** — trusts results, not restraint.
- **Aldwin** — staff cracked. Respected, cautious.
- **Edwyn** — warmth thinner. Rebuilding.
- **Pip** — Ley-dependent wizard. Level 1. Near Kenji = powerful.
- **Ryn** — Scroll savant. Level 1. Needs live casting exposure.
- **Brindle** — guild operations. Pragmatic.
- **Kael (guild)** — guild fighter. Leading Delve salvage. Loyal.

### Unresolved Threads
- Vael — alive, powerless, desperate
- Council mine response — incoming
- Gear from Maren — due tomorrow
- 50 GP bounty — Garrett delivering
- Delve armory — being stripped by guild

---

## 🎯 DM PACING

- **2-3 hours = no filler.** Every combat advances plot or forces moral choice.
- **1 major choice per act.** Consequences cascade.
- **NPCs react in real time.** Dren hears about the mine before Kenji arrives. Senna hears about the 339 freed. Mordecai recognizes the architecture.
- **Bleakmoor contracts are the breadcrumb trail.** The world pushes toward the threat.
- **Mordecai not revealed until Act 2.** Act 1 = "something is wrong." Act 2 = "someone is doing this." Act 3 = "this is who and why."
- **The mirror moment:** When Kenji meets Mordecai and hears his story, the DM plays it straight. No villain speech. A tired, burned man explaining why. The player should feel uncomfortable.

---

## 🚨 CRITICAL DM REMINDERS

- Apply ALL rules from dm_rules_and_tracking.md — Living World, Player Agency, Encounter Philosophy, Economy, No Repetition.
- Morality tracking is SILENT. The player sees NPCs responding differently, never the axis.
- Mordecai is not evil. He is wrong. The distinction matters.
- Dren ignores charisma entirely. Pretty Privilege does not work on a man who spent ten years in a quarry. He reads hands, not faces.
- Senna is Kenji's equal in a different discipline. Not inferior, not superior. Peer.
- The arena is a moral trap. The refugees are visible. The choice is not obvious.
- Kenji can't read. Contracts. Research notes. The inscription above the primary gate. The most powerful man in the story still needs someone to read for him.

**DM NOTES — Kenji combat modifiers:**
- Cross-Guard (+4 AC) requires two weapons. Emberfrost = one weapon = no cross-guard.
- Power of Friendship (+2 attack) requires friendly observer. Remove if solo.
- Frost Fang heal = 25% of total damage × 2 (Metabolism) = 50%. Overflow → temp HP (cap = max HP).
- Emberfang: 1d8+2 slash + 1d6 fire. Passive Ignite CON DC 15 or burn 1d6/rd.
- Emberfrost combined: both blade damages per hit. No cross-guard/cage. Cyclone 30ft returning. Horizon Arc 30ft AOE 1/combat.
- Somnus Knife: 0 doses remaining. Bittershade: 0 doses remaining.
- **This dict is the L12 snapshot — Spell Save DC 18.** For current Kenji use the Level 18 block above (DC 19).
- **Haste max attack economy: Twin Fang 2 + Stride 1 + Haste 2 = 5 attacks/round. Concentration is the price.**
- **Giant's Throw + God Sight: thrown range 240/360ft. Counter Throw = free ranged attack on enemy miss (2rd CD).**
- **Full buff stack (pre-combat at ley line): God Sight + Stride + Haste + Edge + Frost Fang + Giant's Throw = all legal simultaneously. Haste requires concentration tracking.**
- **Cyclone IS a thrown weapon. Giant's Throw applies: range (30+60 God Sight) × 3 = 270ft. Damage × 1.5. Counter Throw works with Cyclone.**

---

## SENNA — The Ashen Fist (Azarinth Healer)

> **Late story scaling:** tournament arc pushes HP **261+** and changes resistances (e.g. poison immunity, charm immunity). Adjust `max_hp`, `encounters`, and `resistances` from the Book 2 DM tracking section in this file when fighting Senna at full scaling.

```python
SENNA = {
    "name": "Senna",
    "max_hp": 198, "ac": 13,  # early-arc template: post-encounter 1 scaling 180 × 1.10
    "stats": {"str": 3, "dex": 1, "con": 1, "int": 4, "wis": -1, "cha": -1},

    },

    "encounters": 1,

    "notes": "Regen 50% maxHP/turn OR purge 1 status. NOT both. Ki Intrusion: 2d8+3 bludgeon + 3d8 force per strike (1 Ki each). 2 strikes/action. Easy to hit (AC 13). Hard to kill (regen). One-shot kills are the threat. Resistances carry over between encounters within 24hrs. 'I'll Come Back Stronger': if she loses+retreats, 72hr later returns 2x HP 2x damage.",
    "abilities": [
        {"name": "Ki Intrusion", "action_type": "action",
         "cost_type": "ki", "cost_amount": 1,
         "damage": "2d8+3", "damage_type": "bludgeoning",
         "description": "Unarmed. +3d8 force (bypasses armor). 1 Ki/strike. 2 strikes/action.",
         "extra": {"force_dice": "3d8", "attacks_per_action": 2}},
        {"name": "Blink Step", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "cooldown": 2,
         "description": "20ft teleport. Dodge one attack. Through objects (not magic barriers). 2rd CD after use."},
        {"name": "Ash Wings", "action_type": "bonus_action",
         "cost_type": "ki", "cost_amount": 2,
         "description": "Flight 60ft. 1 Ki/rd to maintain."},
        {"name": "Ash Shield", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "cost_type": "ki", "cost_amount": 2,
         "description": "+4 AC vs one attack OR +2 AC vs all attacks until next turn."},
        {"name": "Ash Cloud", "action_type": "action",
         "cost_type": "ki", "cost_amount": 3,
         "save_stat": "con", "save_dc": 16,
         "description": "15ft radius blind. 1 round."},
    ],
}
```

**DM NOTES — Senna combat behavior:**
1. Opens aggressive. Charges biggest threat. Ki Intrusion immediately.
2. Takes hits (AC 13). Regen handles sustained damage.
3. Blink Step to dodge the ONE scary attack per 3 rounds (crits, Thunder Strike).
4. Ash Wings if enemy has no ranged. Dive-bomb.
5. Ash Cloud to blind clusters, then punches blind targets.
6. MORE aggressive as fight continues (INT 18 adapting).
7. Retreats if she'll die. Comes back stronger in 72hrs.
8. Each encounter adds +10% HP, +5% damage permanently. Track encounters.

**SCALING TRACKER:**
- Encounters: 1 (Kenji spar). HP: 180→198. Dmg: +5%.
- Resistances carried: necrotic 0% (EXPIRED), cold 0% (EXPIRED), poison 100% (Varn vials, 24hr), mental 0% (EXPIRED).
- Next encounter: HP becomes 217 (198×1.10). Dmg: +10%.

## THESSALY — Wardbreakers Arcanist
```python
THESSALY = {
    "name": "Thessaly",
    "max_hp": 47, "ac": 14,

    "proficiency": 4, "attack_bonus": 7,
    "spell_attack": 7, "spell_save_dc": 15,
    "speed": 30, "base_speed": 30, "initiative_mod": 2,
    "spell_slots": {"1": [4,4], "2": [3,3], "3": [2,2]},
    "disposition": "hostile",  # UPDATE AT LOAD TIME based on story state
    "notes": "Glass cannon. 9yr Academy grad. Crystal-focus staff. Hostile disposition toward Kenji. Ward specialist. Will NOT fight dirty — Academy rules. Forfeits if outmatched rather than risk injury. Book is her shield.",
    "abilities": [
        {"name": "Arcane Bolt", "action_type": "action",
         "damage": "1d10+4", "damage_type": "force",
         "description": "3 bolts per action. Spell attack +7 each. 1d10+4 force per bolt.",
         "extra": {"bolts": 3}},
        {"name": "Crystal Beam", "action_type": "action",
         "cost_type": "spell_slot", "slot_level": 2,
         "damage": "4d8", "damage_type": "force",
         "save_stat": "dex", "save_dc": 15,
         "description": "Focused beam. DEX DC 15. Full on fail, half on save."},
        {"name": "Ward Barrier", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "cost_type": "spell_slot", "slot_level": 1,
         "description": "Reduce incoming damage by 1d10+4."},
        {"name": "Force Wall", "action_type": "action",
         "cost_type": "spell_slot", "slot_level": 2,
         "description": "10ft transparent barrier. Blocks movement and projectiles. 1 min."},
        {"name": "Dispel", "action_type": "action",
         "cost_type": "spell_slot", "slot_level": 3,
         "description": "Remove one magical effect. Can target buffs on enemies or debuffs on allies."},
        {"name": "Arcane Shield", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "description": "+3 AC vs one attack. No slot cost. 1/round.",
         "extra": {"ac_bonus": 3}},
    ],
}
```

**DM NOTES — Thessaly combat behavior:**
1. Stays at range. Always. 30ft+ if possible.
2. Opens with Arcane Bolt x3. Tests defenses.
3. If bolts can't penetrate AC, switches to Crystal Beam (save-based, ignores AC).
4. Force Wall to create distance if enemy closes.
5. Ward Barrier reaction on big incoming hits.
6. Dispel if enemy has visible buffs she can identify (Arcana INT +8).
7. Will NOT take a beating. Forfeits before she drops below 50% HP in a spar.
8. In real combat (not spar): much more vicious. Uses terrain, combo spells, targets weaknesses.

         "description": "Melee. From stealth = auto-crit. Grapple on hit.",
         "extra": {"grapple_on_hit": True, "auto_crit_from_stealth": True}},
        {"name": "Glass Skin", "action_type": "passive",
         "description": "Invisible while stationary. ADV stealth. Radiant breaks for 1 round."},
        {"name": "Drag", "action_type": "bonus_action",
         "description": "Grappled target dragged 15ft. STR contest."},
        {"name": "Shatter Burst", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "cost_type": "charge", "max_charges": 1, "charges": 1,
         "save_stat": "con", "save_dc": 16, "damage": "3d6", "damage_type": "piercing",
         "description": "When hit: explodes 10ft. CON DC 16. Reforms next turn."},
    ],
}
```
**DM NOTES — Glass Stalker behavior:**
1. Always targets the squishiest party member first. NOT Kenji.
2. Uses grappled target as cover against ranged attacks (+5 AC effective).
3. Drags grappled target up walls/ceilings to deny melee reach.
4. Shatter Burst is a reaction — punishes the first hit, damages nearby allies.
5. After Shatter Burst, reforms invisible next round if not hit by radiant.
6. **ALWAYS run ambush_check() before this encounter. God Sight advantage applies.**

## ⚔️ ALLY COMBAT STATS

### Sera — Darkblades Captain (Elemental Battle Mage)
```python
SERA = {
    "name": "Sera", "max_hp": 65, "ac": 16,
    "stats": {"str": 2, "dex": 3, "con": 1, "int": 2, "wis": 2, "cha": 0},
    "proficiency": 3, "attack_bonus": 6, "spell_attack": 5, "spell_save_dc": 13,
    "speed": 30, "initiative_mod": 2,
    "disposition": "close",
    "notes": "Battle mage. Rapier + elemental evocation. NEW: Rapier of Arrest + Breach Shard. Breach Shard upcasts ALL elemental evocation +1 tier. Three years of siphon drain — now she has her magic back and it hits harder than ever.",
    "spell_slots": {"1": [4,4], "2": [3,3], "3": [2,2]},
    "abilities": [
        {"name": "Rapier Strike", "damage": "1d8+6", "damage_type": "piercing",
         "description": "Rapier of Arrest: +3 finesse. 2 attacks per action. On CRIT: target CON DC 16 or paralyzed 1 round."},
        {"name": "Fireball", "damage": "8d6", "damage_type": "fire",
         "cost_type": "spell_slot", "slot_level": 2,
         "save_stat": "dex", "save_dc": 13,
         "description": "L2 slot → hits as L3 (Breach Shard). 20ft radius. DEX save. Half on save. The room catches fire."},
        {"name": "Lightning Bolt", "damage": "8d6", "damage_type": "lightning",
         "cost_type": "spell_slot", "slot_level": 2,
         "save_stat": "dex", "save_dc": 13,
         "description": "L2 slot → hits as L3 (Breach Shard). 100ft line. DEX save. Half on save."},
        {"name": "Ice Cone", "damage": "8d8", "damage_type": "cold",
         "cost_type": "spell_slot", "slot_level": 3,
         "save_stat": "con", "save_dc": 13,
         "description": "L3 slot → hits as L4 (Breach Shard). 60ft cone. CON save. Half on save. Targets that fail are slowed 10ft for 1 round."},
        {"name": "Annihilation Ray", "damage": "3d10", "damage_type": "void",
         "cost_type": "charge", "max_charges": 3, "charges": 3,
         "description": "Breach Shard. 60ft. Spell attack. 3/combat. Pure abyssal energy. No save — attack roll."},
        {"name": "Parry", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "description": "Reduce melee damage by 1d8+3."},
    ],
}
```
**DM NOTES — Sera combat:**
1. Opens at range — Fireball for groups, Lightning Bolt for lines, Ice Cone if they rush her.
2. Breach Shard makes every elemental spell hit one tier above its slot. L2 Fireball = L3 damage (8d6).
3. Closes to rapier range when spell slots run low or when she reads an opening.
4. Rapier of Arrest crit paralyze is her finisher — set up with Ice Cone slow, then rapier.
5. Annihilation Rays are her trump cards — 3d10 void with no save, just attack roll. Three per fight.
6. She's a DIFFERENT fighter than Book 1. The drain is over. The magic is back. She's showing what a battle mage actually looks like when she's not running on fumes.
7. In the tournament: expect Fireball in Round 1 to end it fast. Ashwood (pure martial, no magic resist) won't survive the opening volley.

### Varn — Wardbreaker Tank (Half-Orc Greatshield Fighter)

         "action_type": "bonus_action",

    ],
    "morale_threshold": 0.0,

```
**DM NOTES — Varn combat:**
1. Walks forward. Shield up. Doesn't rush. Lets them come to him.
2. Shield Bash → prone → Warhammer with advantage. His bread and butter.
3. Grapples faster opponents to negate speed advantage.
4. Shield Wall reaction every round — effectively 1d12+4 damage reduction per hit.
5. Relentless Endurance means you have to kill him TWICE.
6. Silent. No taunts. No reactions. Just shield, hammer, forward.

### Vael — Ironveil Captain (Abjuration Specialist) — TOURNAMENT VERSION
```python
VAEL = {

         "description": "60ft. Spell attack. His only offense. Precise, not powerful."},
        {"name": "Arcane Ward", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "description": "Reaction: absorb up to 15 damage from any source. Refreshes each round."},
        {"name": "Ward Cage", "action_type": "action", "save_stat": "int", "save_dc": 18,
         "description": "Target INT DC 18 or restrained in force cage for 2 rounds. Concentration."},
        {"name": "Counterspell", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "cooldown": 1,
         "description": "Negate one spell. Auto-success on L3 and below. Check for higher."},
        {"name": "Reflect Ward", "cost_type": "charge", "max_charges": 2, "charges": 2,
         "description": "When hit by spell: reflect half damage back at caster. 2/combat."},
    ],
}
```
**DM NOTES — Vael combat:**
1. NEVER engages melee. Stays at range. Wards absorb everything.
2. Ward Cage is his win condition — lock opponent down, chip with Force Shards.
3. Counterspell shuts down casters. Reflect Ward punishes them.
4. Low HP, low damage. Wins by making opponents unable to act.
5. Against melee fighters (Sera): Ward Cage + distance = she can't reach him.
6. Against casters: Counterspell + Reflect = they hurt themselves.
7. Weakness: sustained physical pressure overwhelms ward refresh rate.

### Dren Valdric — Lord of Ironholt (Tournament Version, Holding Back)
```python
DREN = {
    "name": "Dren Valdric", "max_hp": 250, "ac": 19,
    "stats": {"str": 4, "dex": 3, "con": 4, "int": 3, "wis": 3, "cha": 3},
    "proficiency": 6, "attack_bonus": 10, "spell_attack": 9, "spell_save_dc": 17,
    "speed": 35, "initiative_mod": 3,
    "theme": "system",
    "legendary_resistances": 1,
    "disposition": "neutral",
    "notes": "Richter from The Land. Multi-class monster. Fighter/mage/crafter/rogue. In tournament he's HOLDING BACK — showing maybe 40% of his real power. Wants to evaluate Kenji, not destroy him. CR 17 real, fighting at maybe CR 12-13 in the ring.",
    "abilities": [
        {"name": "Ironholt Blade", "damage": "2d8+4", "damage_type": "slashing",
         "description": "Custom weapon. +4. 3 attacks per action. Each can trigger a different effect."},
        {"name": "System Strike", "action_type": "bonus_action", "damage": "2d6", "damage_type": "force",
         "description": "Bonus action. Exploit a weakness identified through combat analysis. +2d6 force."},
        {"name": "Adaptive Counter", "action_type": "reaction", "is_reaction": True,
         "description": "After being hit by an attack type once, gain +3 AC against that type for remainder of fight. Stacks."},
        {"name": "Phase Step", "action_type": "free", "cooldown": 2,
         "description": "Teleport 15ft. 2rd cooldown. Dodges one attack completely."},
        {"name": "Evaluate", "action_type": "passive",
         "description": "Each round, Dren identifies one of the opponent's abilities and develops a counter. By Round 3, he's adapted to the opponent's primary strategy."},
    ],
    "phases": [
        {"trigger_hp_pct": 0.40, "new_ac": 21, "description": "Impressed. Stops holding back. +2 AC. Attacks get serious."},
    ],
}
```
**DM NOTES — Dren tournament behavior:**
1. Round 1-2: Testing. 3 attacks per round but not using full power. Reading Kenji.
2. Adaptive Counter stacks — by Round 3, Kenji's primary attack type has +3/+6/+9 AC against it.
3. Phase Step dodges Cyclone or big hits every 2 rounds.
4. System Strike exploits whatever weakness Dren identifies — changes each round.
5. At 40% HP: stops holding back. Phase transition. This is the REAL fight.
6. Evaluate is the key mechanic — Dren gets SMARTER each round. The longer the fight goes, the harder he is.
7. He has 1 Legendary Resistance — one "no" to a save he'd otherwise fail (Thunder Strike stun, charm, etc.)
8. **Dren is NOT trying to win at all costs. He's evaluating the ArchMagus. If Kenji impresses him, Dren has plans.**

```
ROUND 1 (12→6):
  Bout 1: Kenji vs Greave (Iron Champion)
  Bout 2: Sera vs Ashwood (Duelist)
  Bout 3: Senna vs Torr (Pit Fighter)
  Bout 4: Varn vs Kessa (Twin-blade Dancer)

  Bout 7: Senna vs Varn
  Bout 8: Sera vs Vael
  Bout 9: Kenji vs Dren Valdric

ROUND 3 — FINALS:
  Three winners. Bracket TBD based on results.

RULES:
  - Yield, unconscious, or ring out = loss
  - Killing DISQUALIFIES the combatant
  - Healing between rounds permitted
  - Enchanted weapons permitted
  - Don't destroy the Coliseum
```

## Novel manuscript alignment

In `Kenji_story_book2.md`, *The Sundered Gate* chapters are numbered sequentially **8–13** (Pipeline → Combat Operations → Iron Coliseum ×2 → Champion). Older notes may say “Chapter Eleven” for what is now **Chapter Ten** (Combat Operations). The duplicate Pipeline block that sat under a second “Chapter Nine” heading was merged into Chapters Eight and Nine in the novel text.
